Her coat, which is embellished with the K Corp. logo on its left sleeve and fitted with her ID below the right breast, is visibly several sizes too large.

### Personality
Shrenne is a straightforward, judgemental person who takes her work very seriously. While more amiable to the Sinners and her coworkers, she holds a rivalry with Dongrang and Samjo's department and tends to treat them harshly, supplying them with a collection of quips. Dongrang claims that "visiting [him] to hurl hurtful words takes up much of her daily routine". Her tendency to look down on the people around her generally leads to self-isolation, however, Shrenne is not entirely opposed to forming friendships, as shown through the strong bond she held with Ran. When it comes to more serious topics, Shrenne tends to act more sincerely; this includes the initial terrorist attack on K Corp.'s labs, whereas she boldly leads her employees with a voice Dante describes as confident. She also shows a tendency to falter and give up easily when faced with personal failures, which she follows up by going stone-faced and swallowing her emotions.

### Story
When Dongrang brought the LCB into K Corp's laboratory, Shrenne arrived to berate him and his department. She appeared again with Fixers of Rosespanner Workshop when the Technology Liberation Alliance attacks, stating three of her coworkers died afterwards.
Shrenne followed the LCB as Dongrang and Samjo brought them to the L Corp. branch containing the Golden Bough. They were attacked by a TLA machine, only for a member to appear and further slow their advances. Shrenne identified her as Ran before the terrorist sets off a bomb, injuring Shrenne and other members of the group. She rejected the use of regeneration ampules for her wounds, and, realizing the Sinners do not need them, left them behind. This brought suspicion from the group, ending in Dongrang accusing her. Shrenne admitted to siding with the enemy, saying she did so because "the tears wouldn't stop". Before she can give further elaboration, she was sliced in half by a Shi Association assassin.
Postmortem, Shrenne's emails to Ran are read by the LCB. In them, she expressed her distaste for Dongrang and the current era of technology, wanting to return to a time where there is less suffering brought by rapid development.

### Trivia
Shrenne's voice actor, Yi Sae-ah, also voices Ryōshū. She is also known for her role as Myo and Mirinae in Library of Ruina*.
Shrenne's network password is "missyouran", named after Ran who left the K Corp. firm to join the Technology Liberation Alliance.
The name Shrenne (슈렌느, *Syurenneu*) may be pun of *syuledeu* (슈레드), the Korean transcription of the English word "shredded", as in to be 'ripped' or 'torn'. This is likely in reference to how she died — having been assassinated via a vertical split which literally shredded her in two.

---

## Siegfried

### Appearance
Siegfried is a tall, muscular man with white eyes and shoulder-length blonde hair with two plaits. His most notable feature are his prosthetic arms made of an engraved wood or brass-like material. The right arm ends in a massive fist whereas the left possess a normal-sized silver hand capable of firing energy blasts; both are attached to prosthetic shoulders with two thin joints and three cables. Siegfried wears a blue bodysuit with green details on the torso, lower legs and neck and a green domino mask with a yellow border. Additionally, he wears a large black fur coat (with two massive clawed paws still attached) fastened at the neck by a silver brooch with eight small fastenings on the left.

### Personality
Siegfried is energetic and enthusiastic with a flair for showmanship. He enjoys attention, attending magazine interviews, and encouraging witnesses to spread stories of him. He even encourages the Sinners to take photographs of him before he defeats them, despite photos normally requiring permission from K Corp. Siegfried appears to hold no grudges against his opponents, allowing Don Quixote (whom he had just killed) to acquire an autograph. He is rather flippant, teasing Sinners while fighting them and complimenting Vergilius for his sharp tongue after being insulted.
Siegfried tends to speak in an archaic and formal fashion and refers to his actions has "heroism".

### Story
After the Sinners' violation of the K Corp. checkpoint Taboos, Siegfried appeared before them to handle the commotion. After a brief conversation with Vergilius, he flaunted his overwhelming power and defeats every Sinner, excluding Dante, with one hand in 46.5 seconds, an action approved by Vergilius to teach the Sinners a lesson. He left shortly after giving Don Quixote his autograph, going off to attend a magazine interview.

### Trivia
Siegfried is inspired by Sigurd, also known as Siegfried, a legendary knight from Germanic mythology, prominently featured in the epic poem the Nibelungenlied*.
In the *Nibelungenlied*, Siegfried is a valiant knight who has become invulnerable after slaying a dragon and bathing in its blood, but he is eventually defeated by the warrior Hagen, who knew of a spot in Siegfried's body that hadn't been touched by the dragon's blood, and was still vulnerable.
Siegfried was first alluded to in a tweet by the Limbus Company Twitter account in 2021. The tweet features a conversation between Gebura and Roland who talk about the strongest Fixers in the City. Several names are mentioned, including Sieg (지크, *ji-keu*).
Hagen (Hangul: 하겐, *ha-gen*), the warrior who kills Siegfried in the *Nibelungenlied* is also mentioned, although he has not yet been referenced in *Limbus Company*.
Siegfried's autobiography is titled "A Hero Should Keep Smiling Until Their Last".[1]

---

## Smee

### Appearance
Smee wears a uniform styled in typical fashion of the Twinhook Pirates, one with a large-brimmed hat with a golden trim along its brim. She has long, white hair affixed out of her face via a middle part. She has half-lidded eyes with violet pupils and wears red lipstick. Around her waist, she has a large belt that holds a hook-hand that she wears over one of her hands whilst in combat. In her left hand, she wields a wide-barreled pistol with ornate gold patterning.

### Personality
Smee is a cocky pirate emboldened by her seemingly infinite power and control over the U Corp. Backstreets, though this is quickly refuted after combat with her. Despite her cool-headed and arrogant attitude, once she is defeated she begins to panic, using her status as a protected client of the Middle as leverage for why the Sinners should not kill her. She is quite bored of her position due to the prolonged distance of her crew's Captain.

### Story
While trying to track down the lost LCCB members who had been taken hostage by the Twinhook Pirates, the Sinners found their way to the Marlin Port Club in search of the Syndicate leader. While the Captain was not actually there, Smee - the first mate - is, and she explained that she not only runs the club but also was the one who came up with the idea of expanding the Syndicate's business ventures into extorting money from people by taking 'guests' hostage. Smee agreed to give the LCB the information on where the missing LCCB Team Leader is being held in exchange for Ishmael telling her all the information she knows about Queequeg. Ishmael was unable to tell Smee anything, so fighting ensues.
After the battle, Smee was left heavily injured, informing the Sinners that the Middle has her under their protection. Due to this, and the fact they know Queequeg, who Smee reveals had quit the Middle some years ago, the Middle will hunt them down if they harm Smee any further. Ishmael was unbothered by this threat, instead choosing to continue with her plan to kill her. Smee finally admitted the location of the LCCB member but Ishmael's decision does not change. Dante attempted to talk Ishmael down, but she disregarded their words entirely and strikes at Smee. Luckily for Smee, Dante stepped in to take the hit and, after a brief argument amongst the LCB, they decided to spare Smee's life and leave the club to continue their mission.

### Trivia
Smee is based off of the character of the same name from the 1904 play Peter Pan; or, the Boy Who Wouldn't Grow Up and 1911 novel Peter and Wendy*, both penned by J. M. Barrie.
In the novel Mr. Smee is not the first mate, instead being the boatswain of the *Jolly Roger*. The Disney adaptation of Peter Pan helped popularize the change of his role in the crew.

---

## Sonya

### Appearance
Sonya is a tall man of pale complexion. He has short, messy white hair that frames his face, with bangs swept over his forehead, and intense purple eyes. He wears layered clothing, consisting of a black vest and a grey tailcoat that reaches his calves, and white pants. He wears an ammunition belt around his right thigh, and a black belt around his waist and shoulder, from which hangs a long broadsword with a golden tassel. Around his neck hangs a pair of black-rimmed goggles with orange lenses, and he wears a black and white scarf around his neck and left arm, bearing the symbol of the Yurodiviye.

### Personality
Sonya is a calm, composed individual who speaks in a temperate and confident manner. He is a well-read and intelligent man, as well as a proficient spokesperson capable of rallying people under a just cause unfitting of the City's usual cruelty. Rodion often recalled him sitting at his desk, immersed in his studies. Additionally, he is noted to have spread the Yurodiviye throughout every Nest in the City, possessing a wide variety of connections.
Despite his reserved attitude, Sonya possesses a great passion: a dream of destroying the systems of the City which exploit the lower class, offering true liberation to the misfortunate by distributing wealth to all of those in need. In the pursuit of this dream, he is more than willing to accept costs and losses—including the deaths of his own men—seeing them as inevitable sacrifices in the makings of progress towards his goal. In contrast to Rodya, who grew hotheaded and desperate in the face of her people's suffering, Sonya is characterized as exceedingly patient, calculating, and future-oriented. While Rodya criticized him for planning endlessly without actually helping anyone in need, Hermann instead considered Sonya to be unlike most idealists who are all theory and no action.
Rodya was disgusted by Sonya's passivity, which he justifies as "waiting for the right moment" to change the world. However, Intervallo IV: Timekilling Time suggests that he has made impressive strides towards realizing the Yurodiviye's goal of wealth equality by staying true to these methods. Despite this, Timekilling Time also paints a somewhat questionable image of Sonya. The members of his Syndicate are shown to refer to him as "Saint" and look to him very highly, without any concern as to his intentions or methods, lending to a cult-like impression in to contrast to his stated dream for the City's people to be equal. His interactions with Rodion in Canto II also come off as somewhat haughty, acting as if he were superior to her. Here, Sonya is dismissive of Rodya's own accounts and feelings, overwriting them with his own unshakeable interpretation of the narrative. A petty and arrogant side to his personality is further established by his decision to bring up her lack of mark and therefore incompetence as soon as she started to get the best of him in their conversation, demonstrating that Sonya is ultimately far from the perfect figure he presents himself as.

### Story
**Prior to Limbus Company***

Coming from District 25, he was described as a country boy by Rodya and apparently never had a good relationship with money. Similarly, he tried to keep Rodya away from money and gambling, but ultimately failed.
Much of his life prior to founding Yurodiviye is unknown, but it's said that he had always been a dreamer, with the wish to abolish the system of oppression towards the poor and give everyone a right to psychological and intellectual delights regardless of class.

**Canto II: The Unloving**

Sonya is one of the four Syndicate leaders gambling for the chance at taking control over the J Corp. casino and the Golden Bough found inside. He arrived late to the game and spent a moment catching up with Rodion about the status of the Yurodiviye before the game begins. The reason he wants the Golden Bough is the same reason he founded his Syndicate: to destroy the system of oppression and exploration caused by those who hoard the wealth.
During the final round of the game, Rodya made a suspicious move, causing the Tieqiu Boss to accuse her of cheating. Sonya asked to check her arm for a Wish sticker, but the boss of the Tieqiu Crew insisted on checking it himself, given the fact that Sonya and Rodion knew each other and therefore might be working together. It turned out that she did not use any Wishpower, asking what will happen to a player who accused another of cheating. Sonya answered with a demonstration, a trash compactor quickly crushing the Tieqiu boss flat. He pointed out that this is exactly what Rodya had wanted back when they were both members of the Yurodivye and asked if she would like to return to the Syndicate. Before she can answer, the Sinners crash through the door and interrupt the conversation. Sonya acknowledged these new 'friends' of hers, then declares that she won the game and that he has no objections to her victory before leaving the room.
At the bottom floor of Branch J-03 the Sinners reached a large castle made of ice, finding that Sonya has been waiting there for them to arrive. He explained to Rodion that before she got here there was no castle, simply walls of ice, and that she was currently resonating with the Golden Bough which caused these changes to happen. This castle is now a glimpse into Rodion's past, a confessional for the sin that has been haunting her for years. The two revisited her memories of the cruel pawnbroker who controlled their hometown, letting countless go hungry for the sake of her own greed. The Yurodiviye was doing nothing to stop her, nothing to help the starving children that Rodion wished to save when she co-founded it, so she had taken up the axe herself and killed the woman. While Rodion claimed she committed the murder for the sake of her neighbors, Sonya disagreed and believes that she only did it to feel special. He explains that the pawnbroker was the sister of a member of The Middle, and how, after only a short time of living free and eating well, the residents of the Backstreets were killed in mass as punishment. He offered Rodya a chance at using the Golden Bough's power to create a world free of starvation and struggle, but she turns him down. He accepted her choice the same way he accepted her win in the poker game and lets her retrieve the Golden Bough without a fight.
As the Sinners attempted to escape the Ice Castle Where Neighbors Lie after retrieving the Golden Bough, Sonya shows up once again, this time to provide a distraction for them. Rodion does not trust that his offer comes without ulterior motives, but, given the lack of other options, they accept his help. He tells Dante that "That Child" will be visiting them soon, and Sinclair sees something briefly appear on the man's forehead. Just before the Sinners run off to make their retreat, Sonya informed them that the next time they meet, he will likely not be as kind as he was today, as nothing will cause him to hesitate once he sees a real chance at bringing prosperity to the people.
After leaving Branch J-03, Sonya met with Hermann to discuss how the Golden Bough retrieval went. It had been Hermann who came up with the idea of showing Rodion an idealized world with the hope it would convince her to rejoin the Yurodiviye and, as a result, let the Golden Bough fall into their hands. He confessed that he is glad that the plan didn't work, because it meant that Rodya hasn't changed since he had last seen her, asking if she is going to scold him for failing the mission. Hermann simply explained that she is well aware that complaining will not change the past outcome and she trusts that she will come out on top at the end.

**Canto VIII: The Surrendered Witnessing**

Now assisting the New League of Nine Littérateurs, Sonya reached Hongyuan following the end of the second round of the Daguanyuan Family Hierarch Evaluations as the various factions assemble to aid their preferred candidates. Working under a team of rookies led by Nelly, Sonya seemingly assisted in the extraction of Jia Huan and Gubo.

### Trivia
Sonya is based off the character of the same name from *Crime and Punishment* by Fyodor Dostoevsky.
In the novel, Sonya is a devout Christian woman from a poor family who works as a prostitute in order to support her family, and she is a friend of the sister of the pawnbroker Rodion had killed. Sonya is the first person Rodion confesses his crime to. Upon hearing of the murders he committed, she encourages him to confess to the police to help put an end to his internal torment.
Sonya is a bearer of The Sign. He is able to see the mark on some of the Sinners and Sinclair briefly witnesses the mark appear on his brow. He is also familiar with Demian, for reasons likely related to them both bearing the Sign, and was aware that he had plans to make contact with the Sinners soon after the events of Canto II.

---

## Sora

### Appearance
Sora is a short, slender woman of pale complexion with black, messy hair. At all times, she wears a large metal collar with the Index's insignia that covers half of her face, with chains that connect to cuffs.
As a Proxy of the Index, she dons the Finger's signature white cloak, with a white shirt with black sleeves, black tie and skirt, with black thigh high boots with golden heels. With her Effloresced E.G.O active, her arms and legs are shrouded in shadows, having large clawed hands and feet. She also grows a long, thin tail with an arrow-like end, alongside a pair of horns and a halo—the chains and cuffs are broken in this state as well.
She is also briefly seen wearing the Dimension Shredder LCE E.G.O, extracted from Wayward Passenger, which she stole from a deceased employee. This E.G.O Suit took the form of a dark blue coat and pants with red, fleshy adornments, a dark undershirt and vest, and thick black boots.

### Personality
Sora is a timid and insecure person, often worrying over how others perceive her. She has no friends due to her position within the House of Spiders and, as a result, craves companionship and validation from others. When she disguised herself as a member of the LCE, she quickly grew attached to the employees of Limbus Company and enjoyed having people to talk to, while also lacking the ability to understand that they were only speaking to her on friendly terms due to believing she was a colleague of theirs. These factors characterize her as naive, a trait which also shows in her desire to please and become family with Rien, who clearly holds no genuine affection for her.
Despite her cravings for companionship, Sora puts her loyalty to Rien and the Prescripts above all else, even if it entails killing the people she has grown fond of. Similarly, she remains a devout member of the Index even as the Prescripts guide her life in a direction where she remains alone and unable to befriend others. When her duties don't have to come into play, however, Sora demonstrates a kind and trusting heart that believes good people should be rewarded.

### Story
**Prior to Limbus Company**

At an unknown point in time, Sora manifested her own Effloresced E.G.O, which she claimed Rien was impressed by.[1] This compliment gave her the impression that Rien might be willing to let her stay in the House of Spiders as a member of his family even after Ryōshū's return, which has served as a motivation for her in life.[1] She was also outcasted from the other apprentices during her time at the House of Spiders.[2]

**Canto IX: The Unsevering**

During their attack on the Limbus Company Headquarters, Sora accompanied her master, Rien, in the search for Ryōshū and the Golden Boughs. While wandering, she obtained a Dimension Shredder E.G.O Suit from a deceased LCE member, which she donned. She was then caught under a portion of rubble as the ceiling collapsed onto her and a researcher named Ravi, trapping them both for some time. Sora spoke to him at length about what food they wanted to eat afterwards, eventually leading Ravi to play dead to get out of talking to her.
During their search for the elevator, Dante and their group stumbled upon Sora and Ravi and subsequently rescued the two. Upon hearing that the Sinners were searching for the elevator, Sora exclaimed that she knew where it was and took on the role of their guide. On the way there, she detailed a story about the fake identity she had assumed, explaining that she used to be a member of a Fixer Office before she was scouted by Limbus Company as a potential researcher. According to her, she was a new hire like Ravi and knew little about the situation. She also expressed an interest in Workshops as a way to explain her knowledge of the spiral weapon used in the attacks.
When they made it to the elevator, the group ran into the Pinky Nursefather, Shiomi Yoru, who had the Boughs with her. Upon their encounter, Sora was reminded that Rien had told her to help her "family" if she ever saw them, prompting Sora to move to assist Shiomi while revealing that she was the apprentice member of the Index. Using her Effloresced E.G.O, she accidentally killed Ravi in an attack meant for Dante, causing her to panic momentarily as she clarified that she wanted to be accepted by her master and not be cast aside even after Ryōshū returned to the House of Spiders. In the midst of her fight with the Sinners, Vespa would appear and shift the tide of the battle. After severely injuring her, Vespa left to meet with the LCD while Dante's group moved on to confront the Pinky Nursefather. As Dante began to understand the futility of winning against Shiomi Yoru and preventing her from leaving with the Boughs, Rien appeared, escaping with her and Sora via the elevator. Right before their departure, Sora asked her master to share the password to the spiral in exchange for their kind treatment of her, to which Rien obliged.
Later during Limbus Company's retaliative raid against the House of Spiders, Ryōshū fell into the depths of her own nothingness on the rooftop. There, Rien excitedly drew Sora's eyes toward the scene, and Sora understood that she was being asked to fight Ryōshū as her final test of loyalty to her master. Sora engaged in battle against her alongside Ren, which ended with the two apprentices being defeated and erased by Muga Ryōshū. This resulted in Sora and Ren being largely stripped from existence everywhere outside of Dante's memory.

### Trivia
The name of Sora's Effloresced E.G.O, Procuration, may be a reference to the Combat Page used by Index Proxies in Library of Ruina, Somber Procuration.
According to The Index Proxy - Effloresced E.G.O::Procuration Don Quixote's Identity Story, Sora's E.G.O resembles an unknown 'god of the City'.

---

## Starbuck

### Appearance
Starbuck appears as a burly man with dark skin and long, black, hair that messily reaches his chin. He has a noticeable scar across his nose, as well as dark stubble on his chin and thick eyebrows. He wears a green button-up shirt with several tears and stitches and rolled up to reveal his forearms, with dark suspenders connecting to his large, tan, wading pants. He wears large, dark, rubber boots over his feet. He is also shown to carry a massive, barbed, harpoon.
In the past during his time on the Pequod, he wore his hair up in a pompadour. In Pequod Town, he is affected by the Pallid Whale's pallidifaction, and has trouble speaking.

### Personality
Starbuck is generally a cheery man, immediately offering the Sinners a hand during their arrival in the Pallid Whale. Despite his kind nature, he is greatly devoted to Ahab as her first mate, so much so that he defended her immediately after Ishmael's aggressive nature being directed towards his captain. He seemingly struggles to come to terms with the deaths of his crewmates, something highlighted by The Pequod First Mate Yi Sang Identity.

### Story
**Prior to Limbus Company***

Prior to the events of Canto V, Starbuck was a devoted member of the Pequod, focused on the hunt of the Pallid Whale. He was close to the crew, and is showcased to be greatly caring and honest to the crew, between playfully teasing Pip as well as comforting Ishmael before the hunt of the Pallid Whale was assumed to be concluded. Like the rest of the crew, he looked up to Ahab as a great leader during this time, even though he also appealed to the others that disagreed with the captain.

**Canto V: The Evil Defining**

He was first met when the Sinners arrived inside the Pallid Whale. Soon after, a great amount of acid began to flood the portions where the Sinners were, before Starbuck and members of Pequod Town arrived to save the Sinners and throwing a rope down to the group. As the Sinners closely followed, they arrive to the town led by Starbuck, before Ishmael made an attempt at Ahab's life, spurring the members of the town to fight back. Starbuck made it clear following this confrontation, that they will not allow their captain to be attacked again. Starbuck accompanied Ahab's crew as they traveled to kill the Pallid Whale's heart. He stood by, and possibly even participated, during the slaughter of many of the villagers. Once arrived at the heart, Starbuck battled the Sinners side-by-side with Queequeg and Ahab, only to later be consumed by Ahab's E.G.O, Gasharpoon. He would be turned into fuel and expended in the battle, perishing.

### Trivia
Starbuck shares his namesake with the character of Herman Melville's Moby-Dick, sharing his role as first mate, as well as outwardly showing want to return home.
In chapter 123 of the novel, Starbuck goes down to Ahab's cabin to speak to him, but stops upon seeing a loaded musket, and debates taking it and shooting the Captain, to put an end to the madness of the hunt for Moby-Dick and finally end the voyage, although in the end, he thinks better of it. The scene is referenced in *Limbus Company* by the scene in which Ishmael walks into Ahab's cabin, to find her sleeping with her eyes open, entranced in the thought of killing the Pallid Whale.

---

## Stephanette

### Appearance
Stephanette was a thin black woman with dark gray hair worn in thick locks. In her youth, when exploring the Outskirts, she is seen in a hiking outfit, including a pith helmet and a backpack with various items attached, such as a compass and a telescope; in this time, the left side of her hair was shaved.
In her later years as an Executive, she is seen with a long blue skirt, a white blouse and white gloves. In old age, her hair had turned completely white, and grown to reach below her shoulders; she is seen in a black dress with a gray tie.

### Personality
Despite being a Chief Executive of a Wing, Stephanette appears to have been a kind person and preferred to approach situations with empathy. Her relationship with The Tearful Thing was nurturing, and she took on a mothering role to the Singularity, reading it stories to make it cry even when that method was not the most efficient option. She would take the time to talk with it and treated it as a fellow living being, as opposed to how others would treat it as a tool after her death. In her old age she selflessly turned down the idea of using the tears to let her live longer, instead wanting them to heal others who needed them more than her.
Stephanette was also a deeply curious person, and explored The Outskirts to learn more about the world she lived in, getting excited at finding flowers she had never seen before and loved to exchange stories with the boy she had met beyond The Outskirts.

### Story
**Prior to Limbus Company***

Stephanette travelled into The Outskirts alongside a compatriot that came from beyond them. Captivated by the beauty of The Outskirts, she took a moment away from a conversation with the boy to grab a few flowers she noticed. As she returned to the boy, he had fulfilled his wish, becoming The Tearful Thing. She then vowed to take care of the Singularity.
Stephanette returned to K Corp. with The Tearful Thing, where she would read it poignant stories to allow it to peacefully create tears for the Ampules.
In her old age, Stephanette continued this process of reading the stories to the Singularity, hoping to use its tears for those that truly needed them. She would pass away peacefully, leading to the issue of succession to her role as chief executive. While the role would cause the board of directors to attack one another, Alfonso rose to the role due to her choice to harvest the tears through outside Stephanette's noble means, securing her the vote among the board of directors.

**Canto IV: The Unchanging**

After her death, memories of Stephanette and her past were shown to the Sinners through the Reminisced League of Nine, from the point of view of The Tearful Thing.

### Trivia
Stephanette is based off of the character of the same name from the short story *The Stars* by Alphonse Daudet.

---

## Stubb

### Appearance
Stubb appears with a buzz cut, with the sides shaved down. His face is stern with a heavy brown and large nose, and he is seen with a dark pipe in his mouth. He wears a green large coat adorned with several gold buttons, with a white dress shirt and tie beneath. He wears dark dress pants and boots.

### Personality
Stubb appears to be stern and abrasive. Despite this, he went out of his way to attempt to save Pip, causing him to be bit and later become a Mermaid. Even still, he followed Ahab blindly even up until his demise.

### Story
Stubb was shown briefly aboard The Pequod through the Golden Bough's resonance, scolding the crew during their voyages. Over time he developed a close relationship with the crew, and especially Pip, going as far as defending the younger crew member during an encounter with a Whale, leading to Stubb being bit instead and beginning a slow transformation into a Mermaid. Ahab sent off Stubb to be incarcerated inside the ship, used as a compass to the Pallid Whale, the target of the crew's hunt.
He would be kept in the ship, being managed by whomever would end up unlucky enough to feed the Mermaid. Following the confrontation with the Whale, his status is left unknown.

### Trivia
Stubb shares his namesake with the eponymous character of Herman Melville's Moby-Dick, the second mate of the Pequod. In the novel, Stubb is a man with a long history of sailing, making him always carefree and relaxed in the face of danger, a fact that often puts him at odds with his Captain.
In Moby-Dick*, Ishmael mentions that Stubb is never seen without a pipe, claiming that "You would almost as soon have expected him to turn out of his bunk without his nose as without his pipe," a trait that is referenced in Stubb's design in *Limbus Company*.

---

## The Barber

### Appearance
The Barber is a pale Bloodfiend that wears an intricate blood-red, short-sleeved, dress with a variety of lace and frills. Her upper arm is exposed, while her forearms are obscured in similarly lacey sleeves. Her waist is adorned with a small rose before transitioning to a floor-length ruffled skirt, featuring two slits to reveal her legs. Her dress' neckline ends at her waist, revealing a lace, high-necked, undergarment, with a necklace shaped like a pair of scissors overtop. Her dark hair is parted in the middle, a single strand from the part pointing upwards, as well as a strand of red hair amidst the left side of her hair. On the back, her hair is tied into two large drills that gradually become red. On her face, she has a pale mask with a beak, resembling that of a plague doctor's stitched over her real face. Following her battle, the mask's stitching fails, revealing her starved and decrepit face.
She is seen sporting an oversized set of red-and-silver scissors which she uses for both combat and tailoring.

### Personality
The Barber is an eccentric woman obsessed with fashion, taking the time to give makeovers to all of the Bloodbags of Area 1 to ensure that they look their best and finding it discourteous that anyone would pass through the Area she oversees without changing into the outfits she has made for visitors. She is incredibly passionate about the attractions in her area of La Manchaland despite their lack of success compared to other attractions, something she was once teased about by Dulcinea.
When the Sinners play 'Fantasy Blood-shooting Range', she gives a retelling of the history of La Manchaland's creation, which she appears to have personally witnessed. The Barber sounds heavily involved in the story she tells, recounting the hatred of humans for her kind with a certain bitterness. Despite this, Sansón mentions that there was once a time that she preferred prettier masks and believed that the terrifying masks which the Bloodfiends are seen wearing in the present day only served to scare people, implying that she was once hopeful that La Manchaland would be successful at allowing for a coexistence between humans and Bloodfiends.

### Story
**Prior to Limbus Company***

Made a Kindred by Dulcinea at some point in the past, the Barber lived closely with her family of Bloodfiends in Don Quixote's kingdom. When Bari, an unusual Fixer fascinated by Don Quixote's choosing to remain in solitude that bored him, gradually planted a seed of interest in the lives of humans outside of his castle, The Barber was among the group as they dissolved his initial kingdom, assisting in the creation of La Manchaland. The group battled alongside humans in a war against Bloodfiends, gradually instating good standing among some groups of humans.
Two hundred years prior to the modern events of *Limbus Company*, the Barber was assigned to the role of La Manchaland Area 1's overseer, wherein she would create games to entertain visiting humans who traded their blood to Bloodfiends as means of peace. The Barber was also tasked with creating outfits and masks for the Bloodfiends who worked at the park. While the group initially was comfortable with their new roles, starvation began to set in, leading to growing dissidence against their father who was choosing to starve them in favor of devouring humans. This dissent culminated in the acquisition of the Helm of Mambrino, which brought the amusement park's leader to his knees. While the family planned to make use of their peaceful father's binding, he closed the park with everyone inside. Only once a mysterious Bloodfiend bearing a Golden Bough arrived did they return to their roles with the park re-manifesting, now feasting on the people who entered the park.

**Canto VII: The Dream Ending**

As the P Corp.-hired Fixers and the Sinners travel into La Manchaland, the Sinners, accompanied by Hugo, are assigned to tackle Area 1, her supervised area. The Barber observed them while they battled through the Bloodfiends and Bloodbags in search of the button to open Area 4, only to learn it was located within the nearby shooting rally game. Within the establishment, the Barber began to play the game with the Sinners, acting as a narrator to the story that went along with the entertainment. She was angered by Don Quixote's mention of her name, though the button of the area would be revealed, allowing the winners to push it. The Barber then appeared in the building, asking about the one choosing to use the name Don Quixote, to which Hugo exposed the Sinner. The Barber revealed she had no plans to allow the group to voluntarily pushing the button before attacking the Sinners instead. In her starved and weakened state, however, she was defeated, causing her mask to fell off, revealing her gaunt face beneath. Just as she began to panic about her appearance, Sansón interrupted the happenings and began to take the Sinners on the story of Don Quixote's tales, forcing them into a play. While struggling in the unusual confrontation, Sansón disappeared with the weakened Barber in tow.
Once the party reached the center of the maze-like dungeon, she, alongside Dulcinea and the Priest, revealed what happened to their father when Sancho left, before stating their intent to kill the Sinners to feed him. However, having yet to recover from the wounds she received from before, she and the other overseers were ultimately killed.

### Trivia
The Barber is based on Nicolás the barber from Miguel de Cervantes's novel The Ingenious Gentleman Don Quixote of La Mancha.
In the original *Don Quixote*, Nicolás is the barber of the village Don Quixote lives in, and is a great friend to Don Quixote along with Pero the Priest. In the first book of *Don Quixote*, he and the Priest would try numerous methods to "cure" Don Quixote of his madness, including burning a majority of Don Quixote's extensive collection of knight-errant literature, and going on a lengthy journey to return Don Quixote to his village.
The Barber's adaptation into a female character in *Limbus Company* appears to be a reference to a plan that he and the Priest came up with to return Don Quixote to his village, which involves the Barber crossdressing as a damsel-in-distress to lure Don Quixote out of the "madness from unrequited love" that he was then playing in a mountain range.

---

## The Indigo Elder

### Appearance
The Indigo Elder is a scarred, elderly man with a white beard, short hair, and mustache. His omnipresent cigar glows blue at the tip and is the only visible feature when his hood is raised. He wears a large, weathered indigo raincoat, gloves and gray pants tucked into black boots.
The Indigo Elder wields a crossbow-like harpoon gun made of numerous riveted metal plates and a barbed harpoon, both of which are longer than he is tall. In his first appearance, he also carries an oar.

### Personality
The Indigo Elder is an even-tempered and unflappable Color Fixer, openly making an enemy of the Middle without concern. He's familiar with the workings of the Great Lake, and agrees to work with the Sinners to take down the Pallid Whale. He's also very sympathetic to Ishmael's past encounters with the whale, attempting to offer her some consolation for her past. The Indigo Elder holds a certain admiration for the Whales of the Great Lake, recognizing the Pallid Whale's longevity and obscure origin and announcing his intention to challenge it. He has a deep fascination for the unknown, stating that one of his goals is to challenge that which lies "beyond the edge of understanding".

### Story
**Prior to Limbus Company***

At some point, the Indigo Elder hunted and killed The All-impaling Marlin Whale, one of the Five Calamities. He hunts Whales and Calamities alike on a small skiff made with exceptionally durable X Corp. alloy.

**Canto V: The Evil Defining**

The Indigo Elder appeared near U Corp's Lobotomy Corp. Branch facility as Ricardo, who massacred the Sinners, prepared to kill Dante. He grievously injured the Big Brother with a harpoon before leaping onto the facility to meet them, explaining his arrival was due to him tracking the Pallid Whale. Although Ricardo warned him his action will cause him to make an enemy of the Middle, he remains steadfast, and Ricardo is forced to flee.
Once aboard Mephistopheles, the Elder discussed the hunting plan, rejecting the use of the busboat for the task as it is too loud and conspicuous, and warns Dante that turning back the clock is not an option against the Whale. The Sinners and Indigo Elder, in their respective skiffs, eventually encountered the Pallid Whale, who the Elder isolated from the other Whales with bait. As the Sinners row into its maw, he stayed topside to occupy the Calamity.
As the Pallid Whale collapsed after being killed by Ishmael, the Indigo Elder breached its skin and lowers a rope to rescue the Sinners. Once everyone is returned to Mephistopheles, he informed Vergilius of his intention to stay on the Great Lakes and hunt the remaining three Calamities.

### Trivia
The Indigo Elder is a reference to Santiago, the main character of the 1952 novel *The Old Man and the Sea* by Ernest Hemingway. In the novel, Santiago is an aging fisherman who catches a giant marlin after a long struggle, but loses his catch to sharks.
The Indigo Elder was seemingly first alluded to in a tweet by the Limbus Company Twitter account in 2021. The tweet features a conversation between two people (possibly Gebura and Roland) who talk about the strongest Fixers in the City. Several names are mentioned, including the "Fixer of the Great Lake."

---

## The Priest

### Appearance
The Priest is a thin man with white, withered skin. He has short, slicked back black hair, and pointy ears. He wears a black suit and a white striped shirt beneath his jacket, and a necktie with a ribbon around his popped collar. Additionally, he wears a dark priest stole, with a gradient going from black to teal, decorated with black and white embroidery.
Like the other Bloodfiends of La Manchaland, the Priest wears a mask that has been sown to the skin of his face, and resembles a goat skull. Beneath it, his left eye can be seen shining bright red.

### Personality
The Priest is a somber but gentle man, dedicating his days to offering counsel for the numerous Bloodfiends populating his Area. Despite his gloomy appearance and low energy, the Priest clearly cares dearly for the Bloodfiends of La Manchaland, growing excited when he mistakes the Sinners for seeking confessional and nostalgically telling the story of Lorenzo, a former visitor of his who the Sinners remind him of.
In spite of his good intentions, the Priest’s faith was misplaced. In the story he tells to the Sinners, he details telling Lorenzo to suppress his doubts and continue acting happy despite his dwindling faith. This behavior is restated by Sansón, who says that the Priest would reach out to the suffering Bloodfiends, neglecting his own well being for the sake of the residents of the park, and spending all of his time rotting in his confessional room.

### Story
**Prior to Limbus Company***

At some point in his life prior to being made a Bloodfiend, the Priest was present during the Machine Purge.
Made a Kindred of Dulcinea after the Machine Purge, the Priest lived closely with his family of Bloodfiends in Don Quixote's kingdom. When Bari, an unusual Fixer fascinated by Don Quixote's choosing to remain in solitude that bored him, gradually planted a seed of interest in the lives of humans outside of his castle, the Priest was among the group as they dissolved his initial kingdom, assisting in the creation of La Manchaland. The group battled alongside humans in a war against Bloodfiends, gradually instating good standing among some groups of humans.
Two hundred years prior, the Priest was assigned to the role of La Manchaland Area 2's overseer, wherein he would host a haunted house to entertain visiting humans who traded their blood to Bloodfiends as means of peace. The Priest was also tasked with listening to the repenting of the Bloodfiends who worked at the park, and providing therapy to them likewise. At some point he would be repeatedly confessed to by a Bloodfiend named Lorenzo, whom The Priest would regard greatly due to his ability to stave off his natural urges, until Lorenzo inevitably failed to maintain his strength, leading to his death and burial. While the group initially was comfortable with their new roles, starvation began to set in, leading to growing dissidence against their father who was choosing to starve them in favor of devouring humans. This dissent culminated in the acquisition of the Helm of Mambrino, which brought the amusement park's leader to his knees. The Priest would take this worst of all, as while he was the first to draw blood, he regrets it immensely and constantly begs forgiveness, even as they continued to stab him. While the family planned to make use of their peaceful father's binding, he closed the park with everyone inside. Only once a mysterious Bloodfiend bearing a Golden Bough arrived did they return to their roles with the park re-manifesting, now feasting on the people who entered the park.

**Canto VII: The Dream Ending**

During P Corp.'s eradication of La Manchaland, Area 2 was searched through by Jia Xichun, Wei, and their group, leading to the area and its overseer being viciously attacked. Despite being assaulted by the enemies, the Priest retreated to his confessional and begin to take in the confessions of other injured Bloodfiends in a state of delirium. While this is happening, his area's button was pushed by Xichun and company. Shortly after, the Sinners likewise navigated to the booth, where they would be surveyed by a waiting Bloodfiend. After this confrontation, they opened the booth to find the Priest inside, gravely injured. Xichun and her men then arrived, looking to torture the Priest, though he first told the group the story of Lorenzo, before suddenly grabbing Don Quixote's leg and asking if she were the one to bury Cassetti, likewise to how Lorenzo's story ended. Xichun, annoyed by the rambling of the dying Bloodfiend, suddenly attempted to end his life, though the Priest was saved by Sansón, who departed with the Bloodfiend similarly to how he had done with the Barber in the previous area.
The Priest, alongside the Barber and Dulcinea, returned upon reaching the center of Don Quixote's Fathoms, revealing what had happened to La Manchaland before attacking the party in an attempt to feed their weakened father their blood. However, having yet to recover from the wounds he received from before, he and the other overseers were ultimately killed.

### Trivia
The Priest is based on Pero the priest from Miguel de Cervantes's novel *The Ingenious Gentleman Don Quixote of La Mancha*. His name in *Limbus Company*, Curiambro, originates from a scene of the novel in which Don Quixote fantasizes about himself, the priest, and a few others living idealized lives as shepherds, and gives them new names more in line with the pastoral genre.
In the original *Don Quixote*, Pero is the Curate (Parish Priest) of the village Don Quixote lives in, and is a great friend to Don Quixote along with Nicolás the Barber. In the first book of *Don Quixote*, he and the Barber would try numerous methods to "cure" Don Quixote of his madness, including burning a majority of Don Quixote's extensive collection of knight-errant literature, and going on a lengthy journey to return Don Quixote to his village.

---

## The Time Ripper

### Appearance
The Time Ripper is a person of tall, slim stature with a discernible steampunk-esque theme to his attire, accessories, and other factors. Their skin is made up entirely of metal, likely brass or gold, with elongated arms and fingers and a singular hole on the right side of his face with an orange gear-like iris. They wear a dark trench coat that is lined in gold with a white dress shirt underneath, with a dark tie that has a pin of a gear in its center. They also wear a dark top-hat that has a pipe coming off of its right side, also metallically lined with two gears near the front of his hat. They wear dark dress pants with dark dress shoes.
It is later revealed during the Dungeon's Fathoms that, when the Time Ripper lifts off their coat, they have several brains in jars connected throughout their body, which all seem to have a separate consciousness and action within the Time Ripper's body. During this reveal, they had two of the brains in their hands connected by wires toward the torso, while the Time Ripper's head was replaced by a larger jar holding a larger brain.
During combat, the ends of their arms (including hands) are seen to be able to transform into razor blades and other sharp implements, which they use as weapons.

### Personality
The Time Ripper's primary personality within speaking to the Sinners is very rational and calculated in their (and their other separate consciousnesses') ideal of carrying out their 'crusades' within T Corp, stating that the process of "killing time" is a hollow representation of what their motives and actions are to T Corp. citizens. Said actions to them are wanting to eliminate the plethora of time-wasting and greed wealthier T Corp. citizens have to make use of the time they were "going to kill."
The Time Ripper's multitude of personalities and second-person narration of their actions are further backed up by the event in the Dungeon's Fathoms, where various brains within the body were revealed. Each one had a varying accent, opinion, or backstory, but all ultimately seemed to want to make their collective goal a reality within T Corp. to make better use of the time extracted from their victims.
Among themselves, the Time Ripper's multitude of consciousnesses make use of an egalitarian system of distributing the time that they extracted from their victims, with each Brain being given an equal amount of time after each extraction. Minor conflicts occasionally arise from the quantity of time extracted being impossible to be divided equally among the Brains, though these are generally ignored or forgotten as long as time remains abundant in the entire community.

### Story
**Prior to Limbus Company***

Before the events of Timekilling Time, the Time Ripper's main consciousness had a close, familial bond with his younger brother. The younger brother had been wanting the Time Ripper to leave the Yurodiviye and relive his dreams of becoming a member of T Corp's Patent Agency. With both running low on time, The Time Ripper and his younger brother reminisced on what could have been if they had enjoyed more time if they left T Corp., and put their name out there. After the conversation, the younger brother had given The Time Ripper his own time to complete an exam to get certified, and had planned to meet his brother near the Clock Tower to return the remainder of his borrowed time. However, due to the younger brother's insanely small amount of time in that day (only two hours), he was too slow to move out of the way of an oncoming car and was killed by the impact, thrown into the air and taking 21 minutes to hit the ground (in the Time Ripper's relative view), a detail which stuck in the Time Ripper's mind. The traumatic death of his brother led the Time Ripper to view the society of T Corp. and the Yurodiviye as a pointless and depressing existence where everyone spent their days in tedium, wasting their own time until it was too late. This caused the Time Ripper to distort, gaining the newfound power to "kill" people's time.

**Intervallo IV: Timekilling Time**

With the Time Ripper now enacting their crusade on T Corp., the company hired Special Investigators to get rid of the Time Ripper, only to result in failure. Following negotiations over repayment for a unique time tax situation, T Corp. agreed to hire Limbus Company as their sixth Special Investigation team. Alongside Dante, Vergilius chose Hong Lu, Rodion, and Ryōshū to carry out the investigation of the Time Ripper. After the Sinners followed various clues leading to the Time Ripper, Dante and Rodion faced them on a street. Following a conversation with Rodion where the Distortion spoke scarily accurate threats on her insecurities with the Yurodiviye, they left to return to one of the Clock Towers. The Sinners gathered further clues on the Time Ripper, and decided to ambush them inside of the Clock Tower. Hong Lu instigated the Time Ripper to slash at him and, to their surprise, Hong Lu was completely unharmed due to the Sinner's time being bound to only Dante. After this, the Time Ripper was defeated by the now-returning Sinners, causing them to flee into their Fathoms.
The Time Ripper fought the Sinners one final time after their trek through the Fathoms. With the fight dragging on, they revealed their actual body, consisting of a multitude of brains within jars, who, as the battle dragged on, agreed to utilize a powerful attack, leading to their last resort of **TimeKilling** one of the Sinner's Time. Due to the laws of Dante's occupancy over the Sinner's time, their final attack failed and used up too much time, and the multiple consciousnesses were losing their faith over the main consciousness and themselves, losing control over its actions, leading to its defeat. After the Time Ripper's defeat and lesson learned by Herbert, they were given a classification by the LCA and taken away by them to an undisclosed location.
In the fallout following the Time Ripper, T Corp. would disallow Limbus Company from claiming the Distortion for research, much to Hohenheim's dismay. Instead, the Wing took them for their own use.

### Time Manipulation
The Time Ripper's unique ability is extracting time from victims that is rent by the "Time Razors" present on their arm. From the victims' point-of-view, they are temporally displaced to a point in the future corresponding to the quantity of time extracted (e.g. if a person living 50-hour days has 200 hours extracted from them, they will be displaced 4 days into the future). To outside observers, victims are incorporealized and held in a state of stasis until they re-emerge, the removed time having come to an end. The quantity of time extracted can be determined freely by the Time Ripper, and corresponds to the depth the "Time Razor" enters the victim's body.
The Time Ripper can only target individuals who are experiencing a sensation of tedium, or is waiting for some event to occur at a future time. To facilitate tedium in potential victims, the Time Ripper modified the local T Corp. Clock Tower to run at half its usual speed, giving the impression that days are twice as long in the area.
The Time Ripper can utilize stolen time for various purposes, one of which is to facilitate it in battle, giving itself more time to act faster than its opponents, similarly to T Corp. Collectors.

### Trivia
There is some ambiguity regarding the amount of consciousnesses that reside within the Time Ripper: their speech makes repeated references to dividing extracted time by a factor of twelve, which may suggest that a total of 12 consciousnesses resides in the Time Ripper, though only 11 brains can be seen in their Story and Battle sprites, suggesting that the aforementioned number is actually 11.
Furthermore, accounting the summoned Unfolded Time Rippers, a maximum of 14 brains can be seen onstage at a time, suggesting that the Time Ripper contains 14 separate consciousnesses.
The Time Ripper's Battle Background incorporates many elements both from the memories of its main consciousness and its victims.
The car and series of silhouettes near the center represents the slowed-down car accident that killed the brother of the main consciousness.
The headless portrait of a man in a fancy red coat in the back left represents the portrait Bumble was waiting to get completed.
The lollipop in the back right represents the unnamed victim that was tasting a 14-flavored lollipop.
The scattered papers in the center foreground possibly represents the unnamed victim that was reading a comic book.
The Time Ripper's character has multiple references to Jack the Ripper, such as his name and him being a serial (time) killer in the London-inspired Nest of T Corp.
The Time Ripper has five confirmed victims (Bumble, the lollipop victim, the comic book victim, the T Corp. Collector, and the Yurodiviye Captain), the same number as the canonical victims of Jack the Ripper.

---

## Tieqiu Boss

### Appearance
Tieqiu Boss has a full body prosthetic replacement, notably a very old model which hardly anyone uses anymore, which makes him stand out more even in The City where such procedures aren't unheard of. His body is made of a silver metal with a large, pale olive, dragon symbol across the front of it, sporting a pale eye in the center. His right arm is a large hammer, while his left is a claw.

### Personality
The boss of the Tieqiu Crew is quick to notice suspicious behavior and will confront people head on when he believes he is being cheated. He dislikes arrogant and self important people, as seen by his comments towards Sonya, and has little patience for other people in general.

### Story
The Tieqiu Boss is the leader of the Tieqiu Crew, a Syndicate of highly uncouth bruisers, and a participant in the game for the Golden Bough underneath a J Corp. casino. The game played out normally until its final round, when Rodion made a suspicious move that the Tieqiu Boss believes to be evidence of her using Wishpower. He called her out on this and demanded her to show her arm, which she agreed to. Upon pulling up her sleeve, he finds that no Wishpower had been used, much to his surprise and outrage. As punishment for falsely accusing another player of cheating, a trash compactor quickly crushed him to death.

### Trivia
The design of the Tieqiu Boss is the same model as the ones the Sephirot had back in Lobotomy Corporation.*
Likewise, the machine used to crush the Tieqiu Boss is visually similar to one used for the purpose of crushing faulty Sephirot in the entry.

---

## Tingtang Boss

### Appearance
The Tingtang Boss is a man with a cocky expression, wearing his brown hair in a slicked-back manner, the sides of his head shaved. He has two dot tattoos on his left temple, and a teardrop tattoo beneath his left eye, as well as having his right ear pierced with a two chain earrings hanging from it. He has a small moustache and beard, with a variety of lined tattoos along his entire body. He wears a green Hawaiian button-down shirt with a silver chain visible beneath it, over dark pants, with black shoes on his feet.
He is seen wielding a hooked shiv, which he utilizes in combat. The weapon has a pointed tip, and an open hole through its handle.

### Personality
The Tingtang Boss is not overly eager to start a fight, instead preferring to make others grovel and beg for forgiveness to avoid being killed. He hastily views others with disgust.

### Story
The Tingtang Gang was one of the four Syndicates competing in a card game for the Golden Bough that lies beneath the casino, with the Tingtang Boss being chosen to play in the game. The LCB met him when confronting the Tingtang Gang with the goal to take them down so they could infiltrate the casino posing as members, as well as to steal some of their Wishpower and clothing. The Syndicate and the Sinners engaged in a battle that leaves the gang members knocked unconscious. Later, when Rodion needed to infiltrate the poker game that the Tingtang Boss was meant to participate in, she poses as a representative of the Tingtang Gang.

---

## Tomah

### Appearance
Tomah takes the form of a young man with blond hair and light-blue eye, with bandages on the right side of his face. He wears the Old G Corp. uniform, with his augmentations include a bug arm and two pairs of wings. As the Golden Bough continues to resonate with Gregor, he gradually grows greater insectile features, such as mandibles and pincers coming from his face.

### Personality
Tomah is a proud soldier that views Gregor as a hero, able to list off several facts about the man with ease and is comforted by the fact that Gregor is on the battlefield, trusting in him to help turn the tide in G Corp's favor. As the loops of Gregor's memories play out, Tomah's augmentations become more visible and disturbing, but he keeps his optimistic attitude and never displays a lack of faith in G Corp.

### Story
**Prior to Limbus Company***

Once working alongside Gregor and the rest of the Old G Corp., Tomah was a bright-eyed private who impressed a strong memory upon Gregor, even despite the dangerous setting of the Smoke War. While Tomah's true state was not elaborated upon, his absence outside of manifested memories implies he was a casualty of the war.

**Canto I: The Outcast**

Tomah first appeared as a delusion formed during Gregor's synchronizing with the Golden Bough, grabbing onto Heathcliff's shirt to tell him and the other Sinners to escape due to the surrounding war. He praised Gregor's augmentations upon seeing them, noting that they were superior to everyone else's. When Gregor stated he never wanted to be a soldier, Tomah begins to mutate, telling Gregor to "take the lead". This scenario repeated twice until the last loop, where an already mutated Tomah pointed to the sky, stating he needs help and doesn't want to die, before being crushed by giant hands of Hermann.

---

## Valencina

### Appearance
Valencina is a tall, older woman with sea green eyes and long, dirty blonde hair that covers her right eye. She wears a Thumb uniform consisting of a rose-red jacket, trousers, wide brimmed hat and untied ribbon over an ivory shirt with the top buttons undone. The right lapel of her jacket has a golden pin with one arrow pointing rightwards. She is seen smoking a cigar, and has black gloves with light palms.
While not visible in her sprites, she is said to have the Relic "the Eye of Odin" in place of her right eye, a mechanical eye with a sea green iris and a segmented sclera.[2] As Ryōshū damaged the Relic using Arayashiki, the wound reopens when Valencina is in its presence, at one point causing a cascade of blood to cover her face. Her death sprite suggests she wears a black eyepatch over it, which has a golden cross printed on the front.
She carries two swords, one being a straight sword with a revolver barrel at its guard kept in a red sheath, and the other, a curved sword with yellow ribbons on its grip kept in an orange sheath. Both have golden, ribbed blades.

### Personality
Valencina is an arrogant, booze-loving woman with a violent, foul-mouthed personality. She has a short temper, immediately taking towards physically attacking Lucio following a perceived failure on his part, as well as frequently harming the young Yoshihide during their training sessions. While she aims to benefit greatly off the cultivation of Ryōshū's abilities, she generally regards the woman in contempt, even while she was still under the care of the House of Spiders. She remains extremely bitter about her expulsion from the Thumb and fall from grace, and is obsessed with making others give her the respect she's owed.
In her moments of lucidity during her deployment in the Smoke War, when she was unable to indulge in alcohol, she became a more committed member of the faction and the House of Spiders, where her verbal and physical abuse of Ryōshū minimized temporarily. However, she was brought back to ruin with her demotion.

### Story
**Prior to Limbus Company***

In her younger years, Valencina was a participant of the Smoke War under the Famiglia Bognatelli, where she made a name for herself as a war hero and vicious killer able to bayonet any foe, killing them before they were given a chance to fight back. She battled against the old L Corp., making express note of her time having tortured the old G Corp.'s soldiers and personally witnessing their decisive weapons. In addition to acquiring the Eye of Odin at some point, the Famiglia Bognatelli gifted her with their personal heirloom sword due to her prowess.
Due in part to her devoutness to her Famiglia, Valencina was promoted to the rank of Sottocapo, though this lasted a measly three days before she was demoted due to her behaviors. She was then disowned by the faction, which withdrew its love for her but allowed her to keep her Relic and sword, believing them to be tainted by her ownership.
Among the five Fingers, Valencina was the Thumb's representative in the process of raising Ryōshū into a "perfect blade". In her youth, Ryōshū was trained by Valencina in her own methods of swordplay, creating a shared protégé across the five factions. Despite her role as a mentor and parental figure, Valencina was frequently physically abusive towards Ryōshū, admonishing her for minor failures during her training. At one point during their time together, Valencina realized the value of Ryōshū, allowing her to imprint the intrinsic usefulness of the girl's role on the possibility of securing her return to the Thumb.
In her youth, Ryōshū once messily devoured a cake, giving Valencina a spiteful moment that stuck with her. Seeing Ryōshū enjoying the sweet, Valencina reminded her that she would smash a cake if she were to see Ryōshū enjoy something so dearly again.
While the Smoke War progressed, Valencina's abuse of Ryōshū ceased temporarily, the woman having become exponentially more focused and dedicated to the warfare. After a ferocious mission against a G Corp. soldier, she returned injured through a door which connected the warfront to the Thumb's Corridor, where Ryōshū happened to have been at the time. Seeing her mother figure injured, Ryōshū attempted to offer her bandages, which Valencina rejected, though spent little time with the child as she was soon sent out for another mission, where higher quality physical therapy would be offered.
Soon after the War ended, the Consigliere of the Thumb ― one of Ryōshū's tutors ― had a meeting with Valencina. Following this, and seemingly the removal of Valencina from the Thumb's official ranks, she returned to being a drunkard.
After Ryōshū's departure from the House of Spiders, Valencina began teaching an apprentice, Lucio, who would be able to act as a mentor to her "Ticket", once she found Ryōshū again. Upon finding Lucio within the Backstreets, taking him in as a method of "saving him", beginning his routine of a daily cycle of training and abuse. Though the task was, on a surface level, graciously accepted by Lucio, he came to despise the woman, considering the odds of one day killing his tutor when her guard was down.

**Canto IX: The Unsevering**

While Vergilius was out with Charon, Saude, and Pilot, Valencina and Lucio ambushed the group with the goal of keeping the Color Fixer occupied during the House of Spider's raid on the Limbus Company HQ. Knowing of Charon's importance to Vergilius, Valencina ordered her apprentice to kidnap and use her as a hostage. During this initial skirmish, Saude's arm was severed as she held on tightly to Charon, allowing Lucio to escape with the girl and then trail after Saude as she ran for backup.
After a short duel between the Sinners and her apprentice, Valencina arrived at the truck where Lucio had tracked Saude to. Immediately noticing the sloppiness of his training, Valencina slapped Lucio and scolded him over his failure to defeat the Sinners, mentioning that he'll be a failure of a "textbook" if Ryōshū is unable to learn anything from him. During her moment of scolding, however, she noticed that Vergilius had caught up to her, and the two began to clash again as he burst into the truck. When their battle came to a momentary standstill, Valencina's Relic eye began to leak blood, a result of being near Ryōshū's sword.
Eventually, the Sinners were able to travel to Limbus Company HQ using the truck's Backdoor portal, and Lucio and Valencina stayed behind to continue distracting Vergilius. While Valencina related
her twisted views on Lucio to Vergilius' relationship with Charon, Vergilius saw through her attempts to goad him into unsteadiness and focused on dismantling Lucio during the battle rather than the Nursefather of the Thumb. Lucio suffered great injuries during this encounter, as while the threat to Charon's life was severely hampering Vergilius' opportunities and cool-headedness, the Red Gaze was still more than capable of ripping through them. When Valencina eventually received the news that the Dihui Star had retrieved the Golden Boughs from the HQ, she gave Charon back to Vergilius and departed with Lucio.
Later during Limbus Company's retaliative raid against the House of Spiders, Lucio was with his master in the Corridor of the Thumb. Vergilius, Rodion, Heathcliff, and Gregor eventually arrived, finding Lucio still injured and Valencina drunk. Telling the LCB to wait for her to finish drinking, Valencina recounted her time as a hero of her Famiglia, remembered for her skills during the Smoke War, as well as her time raising Ryōshū. After some provocations from both sides, Valencina ordered Lucio to prepare for battle in spite of his injuries. Lucio proceeded to fight against the three Sinners while Valencina fought one-on-one against Vergilius; as the battle escalated, Vergilius and Valencina joined the others, and the Limbus Company team's strength begun to overwhelm the two.
When Lucio was wounded to the point where he could no longer fight, Valencina lambasted him and ordered him to continue attacking. As such, Lucio continued onward against Gregor, who had been growing unstable at the use of familiar phrases he'd once heard from his mother. After Lucio managed to land a hit on Gregor, the Sinner again warned him to back down, but Lucio marched ahead, and was run through by the surprise mutation of Gregor's bio-prosthetic arm, which ripped Lucio's heart out of his chest and killed him instantly. Valencina, however, deluded as she was, initially could not stomach the idea that Lucio wasn't just being lazy and continued to yell at him.
After a few attempts to call Lucio back to battle, the reality of Lucio's death set in, leading Valencina to attack Gregor in a blind fury. The two flew off further into the Corridor, where Valencina began to torture Gregor while recounting similar excursions against other bug-augmented soldiers. Despite Gregor begging her to stay back, Valencina failed to listen and continued to provoke him. In a moment of unwilling metamorphosis, Valencina was skewered on a growth from Gregor's arm as he entered a form known as the Roach Emperor, a weapon intended for war. Skewered and unable to move, Valencina was repeatedly crushed between a set of teeth grown along the arm, finally killing her.

### Trivia
Valencina is known to drink Old Parr, a kind of whiskey. This is an actual whiskey, also known as Grand Old Parr, first made in Scotland in 1909.

---

## Vespa

### Appearance
Vespa is a tall and muscular man with pale skin and short black hair with yellow highlights and blunt bangs that cover his forehead. He dons square glasses and has a tired look on his face. In Distortion Detective, he had his hair slicked back.
As a Taboo Hunter of N Corp., he wears a black skintight suit with a yellow symbol that resembles a wasp, black pants and shoes, and a yellow belt to which are attached two weapons―a hwando with a yellow blade and a harpoon created from the Relic Gungnir. He wears a yellow flight jacket with black highlights, which carries the same symbol as his shirt.
After his demotion, Vespa dons an ordinary black shirt and dress pants, and a gray-blue coat with a singular yellow streak running across its left side. He maintains the belt he uses to carry his weapons.

### Personality
Vespa is a serious and calculating individual, almost always acting in a manner that is both highly professional and detached from any emotions. He is well aware of his abilities and limits, frequently giving accurate assessments of how long a battle will take and never attempts to present himself as more capable than he actually is. Thanks to his time as a Taboo Hunter, he is highly observant and intelligent, able to quickly gather the basics of a situation and adjust his plans accordingly. This also makes him very adaptable, and he has a high level of mental fortitude that allows him to do even unpleasant things in order to survive, as seen by him turning to cannibalism to prevent starvation.
Despite this cold demeanor, Vespa has a sense of justice that he tries to follow and does not enjoy killing people needlessly. When talking to others for reasons unrelated to work, he respects peoples wishes when they ask him to not inquire about certain topics and rarely attempts to force his opinions on others. He has a fondness for vehicles and is a skilled driver, and enjoys cinnamon tea.
The only situation that gives Vespa trouble in following orders is when he's made to interact with Syndicates. Due to a tragic event in his past, Vespa prefers to kill Syndicate members rather than walk away and allow them to continue killing others. He has a particular hatred for the Thumb and is barely able to tolerate their presence. When Ezra discussed the Thumb's weapons and the various design elements of them that make them so well suited to taking lives, Vespa became upset to the point of drawing his sword on her in order to get her to stop discussing the Thumb's purges. Even with these struggles with Syndicates, Vespa still ultimately listens to Moses when she tells him to not cause them unnecessary trouble by instigating fights needlessly.

### Story
**Prior to The Distortion Detective**

In the past, Vespa was seemingly a victim to one of the Thumb's purges but somehow managed to escape with his life.[2] The specifics of this event went unexplored in The Distortion Detective due to the series being cancelled, but he is still haunted by those memories and carries a deep grudge against the Thumb and Syndicates as a whole because of it. Presumably after his incident with the Thumb, Vespa found himself in the depths of the Ruins where he found the Relic "Gungnir"—a golden speartip.[3] Through a lucky coincidence, Vespa was able to wield this Relic and he fashioned it into a harpoon, with it acting as one of his primary weapons from then on.
Later in life, Vespa worked his way up to becoming a Grade 1 Fixer, getting numerous augmentations to strengthen his body, and eventually found employment as a Taboo Hunter of N Corp.

**The Distortion Detective**

Vespa was assigned to hunt down YuRia after she violated one of N Corp.'s Taboos, which led him to Moses' Office. Moses covered for YuRia, who hid in plain sight as a teddy bear created by her Psychoment that her consciousness had recently been transferred into. Vespa was suspicious, but ultimately gave them his business card so they could contact him with any information on the Taboo violator and left. The women made plans to flee District 14 right away, but Vespa pursued them and quickly caught up with them and disposed of the Fixers they had hired to protect them throughout their escape. When Moses attempted to use her Psychoment to attack him, Vespa cut off her right arm to stop her and stored it in a preservation cube.
As Vespa's main goal was to destroy the footage that broke the Taboo, he opted to ask Moses about its whereabouts instead of immediately bringing her into N Corp. custody. Moses agreed to take him to the footage and asked YuRia to open her workshop door, but Vespa refused to enter first given how untrustworthy the location was. His suspicions were proven correct as YuRia immediately began to attack him with countless teddy bears that emerged from her workshop, although he fended them off with ease. Ezra then arrived to protect Moses, and her and Vespa had an intense battle that ultimately ended with Vespa being tricked into entering the workshop and being locked inside.
Vespa was trapped inside the workshop with no method of escape for two weeks, and eventually was forced to eat Moses' arm that he had with him in order to survive. Fortunately for Vespa, Moses and her assistants had found themselves in a dangerous situation while in Quercus Village and had to open the door and free Vespa in order to survive. While upset with Moses and her companions for breaking his trust, he recognized the danger of the dozens of Distortions that were attacking all of them and fought alongside them. After the Distortions were subdued, Han Hee-joon arrived to discuss matters with Moses and handed off a letter from N Corp. to Vespa that informed him he had been expelled from his position as a Taboo Hunter due to his failure with this job.
Han Hee-joon took Vespa, Moses, Ezra, and YuRia to one of Dias' mansions to discuss hiring them to retrieve Distortions from within Nest L. Despite their recent conflicts, Vespa agreed to work with Moses' Office for Dias after being promised a chance to be reinstated with N Corp. and the group set off the next day. Once within District 12, they quickly captured the Distortions 'The Laundry of Dreams' and 'The Human Thunderbolt' and contained them within their van's cargo compartment which was created as a dimensional container. The latter's powers caused the van to break down, however, and the group realized they would be unable to make it to safety before the Night in the Backstreets began. After surviving two waves of Sweepers, they were granted shelter by some members of the Thumb that had occupied a home before the Night came.
Due to his past with the Thumb, Vespa was incredibly reluctant to cooperate with them, but respected Moses' orders to not cause trouble. He transferred the authority he had as a Grade 1 Fixer according to the Thumb's hierarchy system to Moses and allowed her to negotiate a deal where they would track down the Thumb's missing ammunition delivery and the Thumb would provide her with information on Distortions in the area. This led them to discovering that the Distortion 'The Marksman of the Mist' had killed several members of the Zwei Association who had just defeated the Syndicate that created the Thumb's bullets. A higher grade Fixer of the Zwei appeared to get revenge for his fallen comrades, and Moses had the team switching allegiances between the Fixer, the Thumb, and the Distortion in order to survive. Ultimately, they sided with the Zwei Fixer and Vespa was able to kill the Thumb members in order to prove their sense of justice to him.
Afterwards, the group traveled to the Nest of the fallen Wing and decided to check into a hotel for a proper night of sleep. This hotel was revealed to be run by the Bloodfiend Elder of L Corp., although what happened during their stay there is unknown as The Distortion Detective was cancelled in the middle of this arc.

**Limbus Company**

Vespa ultimately followed Moses and Ezra to work for Limbus Company's Distortion Department.
Canto VII: The Dream Ending
Vespa was mentioned to be working off screen while Moses and Ezra video called the LCB.
Canto IX: The Unsevering
When the Five Fingers raided Limbus Company HQ, Vespa was in the middle of completing his registration to become a Color Fixer with the Hana Association. Once the forms were completed, Vespa rushed to the HQ to protect his colleagues. He spotted Dante's group first and assisted them in their fight against Sora, before retreating to meet up with Moses' group once the fight was over. After meeting up with the former's group, he fought against Matthias to protect the wounded LCD members, before Matthias called off the fight after receiving an order to retreat.
Later, the surviving members of Limbus Company decided to launch a counter-raid on the House of Spiders in order to retrieve the Golden Boughs that had been stolen from them. Moses and the members of the LCD planned to participate in the counter-raid, excluding Aeng-du who was still recovering from her injuries during the raid.
The LCD, alongside Don Quixote, Hong Lu and Yi Sang entered the Middle's Corridor within the House. The group engaged in battle with Matthias and Kira. Alongside Ezra, Vespa clashed with the Nursefather. Nearing the end of the battle, Kira attacks Vespa and locks him in place, giving Matthias the opportunity to finish off Vespa. To her and Vespa's surprise, Matthias slashes at both of them. While Vespa survived Matthia's attack, Kira was mortally injured.
